  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6d6dc01a-11d0-4a96-b57c-e64b802f7e72'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      initializeSiwa();

She's staying in a creepy old house with her Aunt Claudia, who reads Tarot cards for a living. And at the snooty prep school, a pack of filthy-rich girls treat Rebecca like she's invisible. Only gorgeous, unavailable Anton Grey seems to give Rebecca the time of day, but she wonders if he's got a hidden agenda. Then one night, in Lafayette Cemetery, Rebecca makes a friend. Sweet, mysterious Lisette is eager to talk to Rebecca, and to show her the nooks and crannies of the city.</span>

<div id="review_71394252" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71394252" />
    <a title="Carolyn  Storer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2449271-carolyn-storer"><img alt="Carolyn  Storer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457826767p2/2449271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71394252?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn  Storer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn  Storer" href="/user/show/2449271-carolyn-storer">Carolyn  Storer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2449271-carolyn-storer?shelf=book-list-2009">book-list-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2449271-carolyn-storer?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71394252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16106678141872572164">Ruined is marketed as a ghost story and it is a story about a ghost, but it's not what I expected. It's not scary, or spooky or spine-tingling. It's just about a girl who happens to be a ghost. The plot is quite good and we are introduced to Rebecca, who is the only person (or so she thinks) that can see the ghost, Lisette. They form a friendship, but behind it there is a secret which Rebecca slowly unravels and discovers the truth. <br/><br/>Rebecca is a nice girl, but we don't really get to know her, an</span>
  <span id="freeText16106678141872572164" style="display:none">Ruined is marketed as a ghost story and it is a story about a ghost, but it's not what I expected. It's not scary, or spooky or spine-tingling. It's just about a girl who happens to be a ghost. The plot is quite good and we are introduced to Rebecca, who is the only person (or so she thinks) that can see the ghost, Lisette. They form a friendship, but behind it there is a secret which Rebecca slowly unravels and discovers the truth. <br /><br />Rebecca is a nice girl, but we don't really get to know her, and it's the same with all the other characters. We are given glimpses of their personality, but then they just fizzle out and go flat. They are not really developed enough for my liking. <br /><br />It is a nice easy read, as the writing is fairly simple, but I did find it a little hard going at times, as it is quite slow paced and there isn't any action in the book to help move the story along. The atmosphere is non-existent, although I did get an essence of New Orleans, but the graveyard, which Rebecca frequently visits isn't eerie or chilling. I wasn't riveted by this book, but I did want to find out about Lisette, how she died and how Rebecca was tied up in it all. <br /><br />During the last few chapters things do pick up when the truth is finally revealed and there is a potential murder and sacrifice. But then, it ends, just as it begins to get interesting.<br /><br />Verdict:<br /><br />Overall, this is a nicely written book, but not outstanding. It did keep my interest but didn't grip me. If you are looking for a scary ghost story, this isn't the book for you, but if you want an easy read with a mystery twist, then this may be the book you're looking for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16106678141872572164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16305578915374117868">Rebecca's Dad has to go to Japan for six months and is going to have to go and stay with her Aunt Claudia. As if leaving New York isn't bad enough, she also has to start prep school. All of the girls are pretty snotty and have a high opinion of themselves, being from the richest familys in New Orleans. <br/><br/>One night Rebecca hears voices and sees several of the girls she goes to school with along with some boys from boys' prep school. She decides to sneak out of the house and see what they are doing </span>
  <span id="freeText16305578915374117868" style="display:none">Rebecca's Dad has to go to Japan for six months and is going to have to go and stay with her Aunt Claudia. As if leaving New York isn't bad enough, she also has to start prep school. All of the girls are pretty snotty and have a high opinion of themselves, being from the richest familys in New Orleans. <br /><br />One night Rebecca hears voices and sees several of the girls she goes to school with along with some boys from boys' prep school. She decides to sneak out of the house and see what they are doing in the graveyard at midnight. The group gathers at the tomb of one of the boys, Anton Grey. Mr. Popularity himself, all of the girls want him. Seeing Anton get up to check that he locked the gate behind him, Rebbecca high tails it out of there and gets lost in the process. Tripping and falling she looks up to see a young girl and asks directions. Getting them she starts off again and when she turns around to thank the girl she is gone.<br /><br />Returning to the graveyard she finds the girl and learns her name is Lisette...and she's a ghost. Rebecca makes friends with Lisette and as time goes on she catches Anton's eye. She also learns that a sighting of Lisette could mean impending doom.<br /><br />Pretty good book. It kept my attention, had a good story line, and didn't divert from the main plot. I think it is a good YA read.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124171978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17783933969919518417">Well it was an interesting one. I loved it from start to finish and it was an interesting look at today's society levels.<br/>At first I was a bit irritated that the South was painted in such a mean way, when Southerners are usually quite nice people. Then again I've never met the high society Southerners like Helena Bowman so I can't know if its that bad or not. But I got over it really quick and loved the way Morris depicts ghosts in this story. <br/>All the characters where rich and believable and it a</span>
  <span id="freeText17783933969919518417" style="display:none">Well it was an interesting one. I loved it from start to finish and it was an interesting look at today's society levels.<br />At first I was a bit irritated that the South was painted in such a mean way, when Southerners are usually quite nice people. Then again I've never met the high society Southerners like Helena Bowman so I can't know if its that bad or not. But I got over it really quick and loved the way Morris depicts ghosts in this story. <br />All the characters where rich and believable and it always is a good book in my opinion if it can make me throw my copy against the wall because of its contents. ^_^. The twist was good (I guessed it) but still good and if it wasn't for my two years in college english studying literature I may not have gotten it right. <br />Very good book. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6147674-katieeoh-lacanlale?shelf=horror">horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223182505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10279274797257839701">Hi! I just posted this review on my blog: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://katieeoh.tumblr.com/post/11431373734/book-review-ruined-by-paula-morris'>http://katieeoh.tumblr.com/post/11431...</a><br/><br/>First and foremost, I loved the cover. Its very mysterious and at the same time it tells a dark, witty story. For me I love books that are filled with mystery, horror and suspense. But I never loved books that’s all about vampires and werewolves and fallen angels…whatever. I hate those kind of books. It shifts my mind into something that is so unraveling and simply…weird. I never loved it, just like Twilight, Falle</span>
  <span id="freeText10279274797257839701" style="display:none">Hi! I just posted this review on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://katieeoh.tumblr.com/post/11431373734/book-review-ruined-by-paula-morris">http://katieeoh.tumblr.com/post/11431...</a><br /><br />First and foremost, I loved the cover. Its very mysterious and at the same time it tells a dark, witty story. For me I love books that are filled with mystery, horror and suspense. But I never loved books that’s all about vampires and werewolves and fallen angels…whatever. I hate those kind of books. It shifts my mind into something that is so unraveling and simply…weird. I never loved it, just like Twilight, Fallen, whatever, etc. So this book is just sitting in the corner of some shelves while I was shopping for books two weeks ago and I got interested a lot. Since its about ghosts, its a bit not-what-I-like book, but I purchased it anyway, and I’m happy I did.<br /><br />Well, I can say that the book really is intriguing. This book was as much a historic delight as a ghost story delight. There’s some romance too, with Rebecca and Anton, and some moments where she spend most of the time with Lisette, learning different things about New Orleans and the rich people who lives there. Paula Morris is a great writer because she did that balance between horror, suspense and romance, in a better, orderly manner. Its a great read, and I really recommend this book to those who doesn’t want to be scared much but wants to enjoy.<br /><br />Ruined was exciting at times, frightening at others, and often oddly interesting. It’s nicely written and organized well, and it’s certainly the kind of book that could be an absolutely scrumptious read at night! <br /><br /><br />More reviews on my blog <a href="http://www.katieeoh.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_76694381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76694381" />
    <a title="Lexie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/712966-lexie"><img alt="Lexie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478802017p2/712966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76694381?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lexie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lexie" href="/user/show/712966-lexie">Lexie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/712966-lexie?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/712966-lexie?shelf=books-owned-read">books-owned-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/712966-lexie?shelf=review-blog-pr">review-blog-pr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76694381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12507405972159064078">Like the main character, Rebecca, I knew very little about New Orleans before Katrina. What I did know came from sources like movies, novels, comic books and random historical facts that stuck in my head from American history classes. Pop culture painted a surrealistic view of the city--populated by a people who have lived and thrived on traditions for centuries and Mardi Gras, was the talk of the world. I was intrigued and terrified by the thought of going to the city. <br/><br/>And then Hurricane Katrin</span>
  <span id="freeText12507405972159064078" style="display:none">Like the main character, Rebecca, I knew very little about New Orleans before Katrina. What I did know came from sources like movies, novels, comic books and random historical facts that stuck in my head from American history classes. Pop culture painted a surrealistic view of the city--populated by a people who have lived and thrived on traditions for centuries and Mardi Gras, was the talk of the world. I was intrigued and terrified by the thought of going to the city. <br /><br />And then Hurricane Katrina hit and suddenly the world knew about New Orleans and it was all you heard about for weeks, months and even years later. One of America's oldest cities, so much culture and history swept away by nature. But Morris doesn't hide the fact that New Orleans has a dark underside--not just in its past, but its present as well--entangled with all the glitz and glamorous parties.<br /><br />I found myself fascinated by what Lisette, the ghost, told us about New Orleans and what Rebecca learned on through her independent study. An entire culture of people and lifestyles I never imagined was discussed. I enjoyed those parts moreso then the rest of it honestly. The curse and troubles of the present day were slow to really pick up speed. For a good half of the book there's barely any mention of the curse at all and other then some rather suspicious behavior and statements made by Rebecca's 'aunt' Claudia and father, there wasn't much to tie in with Rebecca.<br /><br />Character motivations were murky at best, shifting and tangling with other secrets revealed a little too late in the game and making many of the characters seem inconsistent and feckless. I liked Anton until Christmas Break, but then he became just as secretive as every other 'old family'. His explanations at the end seemed off center and even a little cowardly. Tradition dictates, but he had spent the better part of the first half of the book proving that he was more than tradition demanded. <br /><br />The end itself was poetic justice in a way. How the curse ends that is. It made me wonder just how much of the curse was true 'supernatural' intervention and how much of it was really coincidence and self-fulfilling prophecy. The first two 'deaths' of the curse could be mere coincidence and given the time period entirely understandable. It was after those that the family began to actively try and circumvent it, so who's to say that didn't bring it about ten times worse?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12507405972159064078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_54746432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54746432" />
    <a title="Angelc" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1445462-angelc"><img alt="Angelc" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1259806586p2/1445462.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/54746432?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelc" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelc" href="/user/show/1445462-angelc">Angelc</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1445462-angelc?shelf=already-own-to-read">already-own-to-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54746432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15064908706412433198">Ruined is a creepy, gothic ghost story, the perfect read for the Halloween season. The setting and the entire tone of the book are so eerie! The book is never too scary, but it gives the reader the perfect amount of chills and thrills.<br/><br/>I'm usually much more into characters than settings, but in this story, New Orleans seems like it's own character. I learned so much about the city's history as well as how the upper class live there today. Rebecca is very much involved with the "old families" in t</span>
  <span id="freeText15064908706412433198" style="display:none">Ruined is a creepy, gothic ghost story, the perfect read for the Halloween season. The setting and the entire tone of the book are so eerie! The book is never too scary, but it gives the reader the perfect amount of chills and thrills.<br /><br />I'm usually much more into characters than settings, but in this story, New Orleans seems like it's own character. I learned so much about the city's history as well as how the upper class live there today. Rebecca is very much involved with the "old families" in town and how their shady pasts come back to the haunt them, so their world is her world.<br /><br />I loved the eerie atmosphere of the old cemetery where Lissette, the ghost, lives. The way it contrasts with the gilded mansions of the old families adds to the creepy factor. And of course, right on the same street as the cemetery and the mansion is Aunt Claudia's shabby shotgun house. The author weaves all three worlds together effortlessly.<br /><br />The Mardi Gras season and parades were so much fun to read about. The costumes, decorations, and all the expense of the Mardi Gras celebration was pretty spectacular. The author really knows her stuff when it comes to New Orleans.<br /><br />Rebecca was a great lead, strong but also known to make a few mistakes. I enjoyed her friendships with Lissette and her perky cousin, Aurelia.<br /><br />This is the perfect book to read on a dark and stormy October night! <br /><br /><br />sent by publisher in exchange for honest review<br /><br />reviewed for <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://inthehammockblog.blogspot.com">http://inthehammockblog.blogspot.com</a><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15064908706412433198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=strong-females">strong-females</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=needs-an-editor">needs-an-editor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=what-might-have-been">what-might-have-been</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=love-the-look">love-the-look</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146050259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4794344171617729669">EDIT: HOOOOOLLLLDDDDD up, does the description really say 'Twilight With a Ghostly Twist'? That is the most ridiculous thing I think I have ever seen. First off, talk about dating this book. Second off...no. No. No. No. This book has absolutely all of 0 in common with <i>Twilight</i>. (And I'm no lover of <i>Twilight</i>. I just really can't think of anything these books have in common that aren't held in common by Every. YA. Novel. Ever.) <br/>.....<br/><br/>I'm soooooooo.....FRUSTRATED. <br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515492131ra/24861932.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book could be the poster chil</span>
  <span id="freeText4794344171617729669" style="display:none">EDIT: HOOOOOLLLLDDDDD up, does the description really say 'Twilight With a Ghostly Twist'? That is the most ridiculous thing I think I have ever seen. First off, talk about dating this book. Second off...no. No. No. No. This book has absolutely all of 0 in common with <i>Twilight</i>. (And I'm no lover of <i>Twilight</i>. I just really can't think of anything these books have in common that aren't held in common by Every. YA. Novel. Ever.) <br>.....<br><br>I'm soooooooo.....FRUSTRATED. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515492131ra/24861932.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book could be the poster child for my what-might-have-been shelf. It dripped with potential. I enjoyed the writing and the overarching plot but the details left me so very, very underwhelmed. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402845262ra/9995415.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It somehow feels worse because I kept expecting it to get better. It had the potential to be <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_" title="The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> good, or maybe even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10866624.Unspoken__The_Lynburn_Legacy___1_" title="Unspoken (The Lynburn Legacy, #1) by Sarah Rees Brennan" rel="nofollow noopener">Unspoken</a> good. By itself, it was enjoyable enough. But when compared to what it <i>might have been</i>...<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521416312ra/25235590.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Maybe it just isn't a fair comparison. <br><br>This is a fairly predictable story that - to its credit - skates away from too much teenage angst. Unfortunately, it accomplishes this by avoiding any in-depth emotions. I didn't particularly like or dislike any of the characters primarily because I didn't <i>know</i> them. I found the plot laughably predictable and the stereotypes (rich, blond mean girl, hot bad(ish)-boy love interest, quirky outsider main character, etc.) frustrating.<br><br>Besides perpetrating literary stereotypes, this book feels like a mixed bag of social commentary on race, socioeconomic status, and post-hurricane Katrina recovery. Here I feel it really had room to shine. Unfortunately, frequent references to Katrina (and Gossip Girl, incidentally) do little more than date the book. In someways, I find this the most frustrating part of the entire thing because it read like a rough draft. With a good editor, I feel like the greater themes of this story could have been drawn through for a more decisive and nuanced reading. <br><br>I seem to be heaping condemnation on this story. I don't really mean to. I <i>did</i> enjoy it. I just wish it lived up to its potential. <br><br>Also ~ side rant since this bugged me from the beginning ~ why are otherwise "sensible" teenage girls always willing to go along with the hot boy? I suppose the answer is 'hormones' but it always annoys me to death. <i>Just because he has a nice smile does not mean you should give him the time of day</i>. <br><br>Side, side comment to counter that rant, I feel like this author did a really good job - or at least as good a job as she does for anyone - making Anton feel like a real teenage boy. He wasn't all suave and cool. He was kind of awkward and clueless and helpless. Now, does that make him a good love interest? I'd say no, but I appreciated it. It made him at least feel more real.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4794344171617729669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94042258?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patty" href="/user/show/2281353-patty">Patty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94042258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1086166944679141955">Ruined <br/>By <br/>Paula Morris<br/><br/><br/>This great book was a true ghost story. I truly enjoyed reading it. It took place in New Orleans after Hurricane Katrina. I loved the historical references in the story. They gave an aura of truth to what I was reading. In a nutshell…<br/><br/>Rebecca has been told by her father that he has a 6 month stay in China. They are New Yorkers and Rebecca is not happy about the fact that because of this she must spend the next 6 months with her Aunt Claudia in New Orleans at a private school</span>
  <span id="freeText1086166944679141955" style="display:none">Ruined <br />By <br />Paula Morris<br /><br /><br />This great book was a true ghost story. I truly enjoyed reading it. It took place in New Orleans after Hurricane Katrina. I loved the historical references in the story. They gave an aura of truth to what I was reading. In a nutshell…<br /><br />Rebecca has been told by her father that he has a 6 month stay in China. They are New Yorkers and Rebecca is not happy about the fact that because of this she must spend the next 6 months with her Aunt Claudia in New Orleans at a private school. Of course the girls who “matter” do not like Rebecca and love telling her as well as showing her that she is an outsider and unwelcome. Rebecca deals with this and sort of relishes her role as an outsider. Her aunt’s house is conveniently just across the street from a cemetery that Rebecca has been told to stay away from. Of course she doesn’t and secretly follows them one night as the “in crowd” gathers to drink a bit and party. This is when Rebecca is welcomed by a mysterious new friend that only she can see. <br />The main stream of the story revolves around a 150 year old curse that affects a founding New Orleans family. The story at this point becomes action packed and mysterious with a reasonably exciting ending.<br />Again…I loved the setting…the story was not predictable but exciting and absorbing. I loved learning about the history of various parts of New Orleans. I would love reading more from this author. <br /></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1020619-educating-drew?shelf=spooky">spooky</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer4397721201339177037">Isn't that cover absolutely gorgeous, if a bit misleading (the ghost in the story is a young black girl and the woman in the picture, well, she doesn't look young or black, does she?)<br/><br/><br/>It being a ghost story wasn't really what pushed me into this purchase, rather it was because the ghost story's setting is New Orleans. I have no ties with NOLA outside of doing the touristy visits. Still, in all of the places that I have travelled, NOLA is the only city that I can still visualize, the only place wh</span>
  <span id="freeText4397721201339177037" style="display:none">Isn't that cover absolutely gorgeous, if a bit misleading (the ghost in the story is a young black girl and the woman in the picture, well, she doesn't look young or black, does she?)<br /><br /><br />It being a ghost story wasn't really what pushed me into this purchase, rather it was because the ghost story's setting is New Orleans. I have no ties with NOLA outside of doing the touristy visits. Still, in all of the places that I have travelled, NOLA is the only city that I can still visualize, the only place where the streets come alive in my head. The smell, sound, and vibrance of the city is a being of its own. There really is something mysterious and magical about this city.<br /><br /><br />Rebecca, our wonderful heroine, learns this lesson in Ruined. She comes to the city unwillingly. Her father must do business in China and a not-really-her-aunt-but-close-enough-that-she-is-referred-to-as-such is to watch over her for sixth months. Rebecca is coming from New York and the change is drastic. Plus, the city is old in tradition and bloodlines, something that she doesn't understand. Not only does she have to be the new girl midyear, she is automatically outcasted because she has no history with the city.<br /><br /><br />Then, as if that isn't a big enough burden, Rebecca meets a ghost in the Lafayette Cemetery. Lisette is trapped in the cemetery and a few other areas and has been so for the past hundred and fifty years. She was murdered and until the curse gets lifted, she cannot move on.<br /><br /><br />The book was initially slow for me. There was something in the beginning that just nagged me, didn't fit, didn't settle. Now, I couldn't tell you what it was, because the book just captivated me. I loved how the author drew in the history and wove it within her own ghost story.<br />Ruined is a great book to read on a rainy day.</span>

<div id="review_62043862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jacqueline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1739429-jacqueline"><img alt="Jacqueline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578724220p2/1739429.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline" href="/user/show/1739429-jacqueline">Jacqueline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739429-jacqueline?shelf=fantasy-paranormal">fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739429-jacqueline?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739429-jacqueline?shelf=read-in-2009">read-in-2009</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62043862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7526647614447926536">I love a good ghost story so maybe my expectations going into this book were too high since I've never read anything by this author before. Needless to say, Ruined was a bit of a let down.<br/><br/>The ingredients are all there. A great setting to facilitate a spooky atmosphere, good historical details, and an unique and well-set up plot with an outcome that wasn't obvious. Despite all of this, there was something missing from the overall story. <br/><br/>Perhaps it was that I didn't find the heroine, Rebecca, symp</span>
  <span id="freeText7526647614447926536" style="display:none">I love a good ghost story so maybe my expectations going into this book were too high since I've never read anything by this author before. Needless to say, Ruined was a bit of a let down.<br /><br />The ingredients are all there. A great setting to facilitate a spooky atmosphere, good historical details, and an unique and well-set up plot with an outcome that wasn't obvious. Despite all of this, there was something missing from the overall story. <br /><br />Perhaps it was that I didn't find the heroine, Rebecca, sympathetic enough. I understand that teenagers are often stubborn and in the process of discovering who they are but Rebecca took these to an extreme. She was just too flaky and, at times, acted like a know-it-all. From jump she spurned all things elite and exclusive and often ridiculed the members of the New Orleans upper-class. However, as soon as she was granted and "in", she seemed to forget all of her lofty ideals. On top of all of that, some of her decisions and actions were just plain stupid. Sure, characters can't be made infallible - there needs to be a discernible growth process. It seemed to me though that, until the end, Rebecca didn't learn from any of her mistakes...<br /><br /><a href="http://www.eclecticbooklover.com/2009/07/review-ruined-by-paula-morris.html" rel="nofollow noopener">...To finish reading this review, visit my blog, The Eclectic Book Lover.</a> </span>

While there she lives with her aunt and attends a snobbish school with established families children. She end up in the local cemetery and meets a ghost, she does not figure that out right away.   <span id="freeText11530422175316778468" style="display:none">Rebecca, a 15-16 yr old teen from NY stays in New Orleans( Post hurricane Katrina) for 6 months while her father works in China. While there she lives with her aunt and attends a snobbish school with established families children. She end up in the local cemetery and meets a ghost, she does not figure that out right away. There is a great and terrible history behind this ghost and Rebecca is thrust into it. She tries to remain strong, but the darkness being reveled is truly shocking, and could change many lives. She meets a handsome and mysterious boy(Anton) and has mixed feelings who Anton really are. Rebecca figures everything out, Now she must fight for her life. <br />Excellent writing,a wonderful historical delight with the Lafayette Cemetery/New Orleans/ Mardi Gras /Voodoo details. I think this is the best ghost book I have ever read, perhaps because of the history of my near and dear New Orleans.</span>

<div id="review_218789042" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218789042" />
    <a title="Lori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2429935-lori"><img alt="Lori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245360566p2/2429935.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218789042?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/2429935-lori">Lori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218789042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15793653163663338351">If you're a reader that's looking for a teeth grinding, heart pounding, sleep with the lights on ghost story, read no further. You will likely be disappointed by Paula Morris' freshman effort, Ruined. Not that Ruined is a poor book - - far from it. But it's more like a ghost story with less calories and a lighter taste. <br/><br/><br/>Ruined is aimed for the Young Adult audience but it's perfectly acceptable as an adult read as well. This adult enjoyed it thoroughly from page one. And while it's marketed as a </span>
  <span id="freeText15793653163663338351" style="display:none">If you're a reader that's looking for a teeth grinding, heart pounding, sleep with the lights on ghost story, read no further. You will likely be disappointed by Paula Morris' freshman effort, Ruined. Not that Ruined is a poor book - - far from it. But it's more like a ghost story with less calories and a lighter taste. <br /><br /><br />Ruined is aimed for the Young Adult audience but it's perfectly acceptable as an adult read as well. This adult enjoyed it thoroughly from page one. And while it's marketed as a ghost story, and there is indeed a central character that is a ghost, there is far more to it than that. It's also the story of a displaced girl, a high school hierarchy and New Orleans history.<br /><br />The New Orleans history was one of my favorite parts of the book. I could easily see the grand old plantation homes with their stately pillars and expansive grounds, as well as the bustling and colorful streets of the Quarter. The very best scene in the book, in my opinion, involved the ghostly Lisette walking Rebecca through New Orleans and the many ghosts wandering around the city, elbow to elbow with the living. It was a colorfully well written passage, alternating between those lost souls who either didn't realize they were no longer living or were waiting to avenge their deaths and the living who inexplicably bumped into something that wasn't there or got a cold chill. It definitely makes you wonder about that other realm, particularly in old cities like New Orleans with so much history. And voodoo.<br /><br />Voodoo plays a part in Ruined but not a huge one and readers who object to the magical or dark arts shouldn't take serious issue with Ruined. By the same token, there is no objectionable language and no sexual scenes. The violence is kept to a minimum with descriptions of the appearances of ghosts as Rebecca sees them - - they appear as they did at the time of their deaths, with the cause of their deaths at times very apparent. <br /><br />I wouldn't say that Ruined is a dark book, maybe a little bit shaded and young readers could find certain sections to be a little much for them. <br /><br />Rebecca is a good heroine; despite being new to the area she seems fairly secure in herself and doesn't seem to be looking for acceptance by the "cool crowd" at school. While she doesn't have a somewhat typical teen attitude, she does sneak out of the house at night which is probably her most serious fault.<br /><br />I found Ruined to be a read that I lost myself in for a couple of days and was happy to do so. I look forward to author Paula Morris' future efforts. <br /><br />On a shallow note, the cover is absolutely gorgeous.<br /><br />Ruined is an entertaining story that will make you think, at least a little, and will certainly make you appreciate the glorious history of New Orleans.<br /><br /><br />Review Copyright © Psychotic State Book Reviews<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.psychoticstate.net">http://www.psychoticstate.net</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15793653163663338351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_79399850" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79399850" />
    <a title="Ellz Readz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2771201-ellz-readz"><img alt="Ellz Readz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294327080p2/2771201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79399850?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellz Readz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellz Readz" href="/user/show/2771201-ellz-readz">Ellz Readz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79399850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4961213831403136807">My thoughts...This book can best be described as flavorful. The reader gets tastes of New Orleans history, Mardi Gras excitement, Haitian magic and an old-fashioned ghost story. The main character Rebecca is thrown into post-Katrina New Orleans in a house with a view of the famous Lafayette Cemetery. Curiosity gets the better of her and she finds herself face to face with a real ghost. Her aunt believe in old magic and voo-doo. She gives Rececca several warnings to stay out of the cemetery and o</span>
  <span id="freeText4961213831403136807" style="display:none">My thoughts...This book can best be described as flavorful. The reader gets tastes of New Orleans history, Mardi Gras excitement, Haitian magic and an old-fashioned ghost story. The main character Rebecca is thrown into post-Katrina New Orleans in a house with a view of the famous Lafayette Cemetery. Curiosity gets the better of her and she finds herself face to face with a real ghost. Her aunt believe in old magic and voo-doo. She gives Rececca several warnings to stay out of the cemetery and out of the way of some of the local kids, but of course, they fall on deaf ears. Rebecca finds herself in the middle of an 150 year old curse. <br /><br />Ruined was very well written. The characters were interesting and like-able. The plot was fast-moving and very interesting. The history of Mardi Gras created a great background for the story. I actually found it fascinating. There must have been tons of research done to complete this novel. There were several themes included in the story including racism. Many of scenes described old New Orleans, an area which is rich in history-good and bad. The ending was a bit predictable, but there was quite a bit of foreshadowing in the form of visions that gave clues. It was very well written and kept me turning pages until the end. <br /><br />As for cons, I really can't think of any. It wasn't very scary, but I didn't open this book expecting to be frightened. I would recommend this book to kids 12 and up as well as adults. It was very enjoyable. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4961213831403136807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText1831011189027802901" style="display:none">This book made me want to see New Orleans intensely soon.<br />The description of Garden District made me google the place sooner than you can day "Mardi Gra here I come".<br /><br />Rebecca Brown's character was likable. She's not the typical 16 year old character that's so desperately wanting to fit in her new surroundings or else she'd probably die of an untimely social death. Its a refreahing changing of yhe typical high schooler climbing the social ladder or the Queen Bee harassing a poor insecure new girl. Anyway I love the story. The mystery started in 1853 at the time of the yellow fever. Morris has also thrown in a little bit of New Orleans history and how the Mardi Gras works and made a beautiful story out of it. <br /><br />The mystery surrounding Lafayette Cementery, the patrician ways of the Bowman, Suttons and Grey will pique anyones curiosity, the ghost of Lisette, and the suspicious involvement of Rebecca and the gap in her family history are the main points of why I finished the book in a day and a half. Morris' writing still made me want to know what's going to happen chapter after chapter. My $16.99 well spent. </span>

  <span id="freeText4065331623977110424" style="display:none">Why do these things happen? Another bunch of trees wasted just to publish this atrocity. <br /><br />First things first. What makes up a good story? Good characters. Riiiight?? Someone you can relate to, someone that you admire, someone that you vouch for throughout the book. Epic. Fail! <br /> Rebecca was a snooty little brat that I can't believe got the main lead. Seriously. "OMG I am so better than everyone. I'm cool, and I don't need any friends." And then she wonders why nobody likes her. She didn't even know the "snotty prep girls", and when they tried to talk to her she just wrote them off as bitches and talked crap to them. What. The. Fiddlesticks! And then when Anton payed attention to her, she's all "of course he would!" as if she were the best and RAWR!!!! She just got on my nerves. It's there, and you can always rely on it. Unfortunately, this one was all over the place. It changed personalities often, and in truth got pretty lame. Can't believe I wasted my time with this one. </span>

<div id="review_180439423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180439423" />
    <a title="Christy (TheReaderBee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2201617-christy-thereaderbee"><img alt="Christy (TheReaderBee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600256562p2/2201617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180439423?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy (TheReaderBee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy (TheReaderBee)" href="/user/show/2201617-christy-thereaderbee">Christy (TheReaderBee)</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2201617-christy-thereaderbee?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2201617-christy-thereaderbee?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2201617-christy-thereaderbee?shelf=ya-paranormal">ya-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2201617-christy-thereaderbee?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180439423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5316642854359689503">Ruined is my very first read by Paula Morris. I was thrilled that it finally came in at the library so I could read it.<br/><br/>The characters are pretty likeable. Of course, there are some you just love to hate anyways. The main character, Rebecca, was pretty likeable. She wants to fit in at her new home and new school, but she really doesn’t seem to care when she doesn’t. I really didn’t see much of a connection between Rebecca and Anton, unfortunately. There’s definitely not a lot of romance in this b</span>
  <span id="freeText5316642854359689503" style="display:none">Ruined is my very first read by Paula Morris. I was thrilled that it finally came in at the library so I could read it.<br /><br />The characters are pretty likeable. Of course, there are some you just love to hate anyways. The main character, Rebecca, was pretty likeable. She wants to fit in at her new home and new school, but she really doesn’t seem to care when she doesn’t. I really didn’t see much of a connection between Rebecca and Anton, unfortunately. There’s definitely not a lot of romance in this book, and I found myself wanting more. I think Anton would have been an easy character to like, if we had seen him more, and knew more about him. The only other character I really liked in the book was Rebecca’s ghost friend, Lisette. The other characters were just so-so for me.<br /><br />I thought this book was an interesting take on the ghost story genre. The back story on the characters and the history of New Orleans was interesting. The plot was simple and the writing style was easy to follow. The place was a little slow in some areas. <br /><br />Overall, this was a really interesting read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5316642854359689503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer183302184" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6727176876987093639">Loved this book! I loved the way the author used the old legends of New Orleans and mixed it in with modern day. I've always been interested in the subcultures of New Orleans. It's city with such history and this book played on that. So much history is immersed in the story.<br/><br/>The characters were intriguing, especially Anton who I really couldn't figure out the whole book. As for our lead Rebecca, I was constantly trying to figure out the connection between her and the "old blood" families of New O</span>
  <span id="freeText6727176876987093639" style="display:none">Loved this book! I loved the way the author used the old legends of New Orleans and mixed it in with modern day. I've always been interested in the subcultures of New Orleans. It's city with such history and this book played on that. So much history is immersed in the story.<br /><br />The characters were intriguing, especially Anton who I really couldn't figure out the whole book. As for our lead Rebecca, I was constantly trying to figure out the connection between her and the "old blood" families of New Orleans. The book always managed to stay one step ahead of me, giving me just enough to satisfy but also to question. <br /><br />The ending came a little fast, but I couldn't stop reading it. It had me turning page after page trying to solve this mystery. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9049935316495766045">I've had this book on my To Read list for a while and finally got around to it. Unfortunately, it wasn't as enjoyable as I had hoped it would be. This book took me over a month to finish. I really should've DNF'd it since I put it down for several weeks and didn't have a want to pick it back up. I was on my last renewal of this book with my library, and decided to finish it up since I had less than 100 pages to go.<br/><br/>I feel like the story did progress quite a bit towards the end, but it wasn't enou</span>
  <span id="freeText9049935316495766045" style="display:none">I've had this book on my To Read list for a while and finally got around to it. Unfortunately, it wasn't as enjoyable as I had hoped it would be. This book took me over a month to finish. I really should've DNF'd it since I put it down for several weeks and didn't have a want to pick it back up. I was on my last renewal of this book with my library, and decided to finish it up since I had less than 100 pages to go.<br /><br />I feel like the story did progress quite a bit towards the end, but it wasn't enough to push the level of enjoyment up for me. The twist at the end wasn't really surprising to me and I disliked the reasoning for a lot of the secrecy and actions that were taken. I was surprised to discover this is the first book in a duology, as I feel like the story is contained in this installment. That being said, I will not be reading the second book, though I may try another book by this author in the future. </span>

<div id="review_105003975" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105003975" />
    <a title="Kathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1244048-kathy"><img alt="Kathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1222131291p2/1244048.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105003975?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy" href="/user/show/1244048-kathy">Kathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1244048-kathy?shelf=teen">teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105003975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6051169393152168466">Rebbecca is sent to live with her Aunt in New Orleans when her dad has to travel to China for work. She knows no one here and is immediately put off by the snobbish manners of the girls she attends school with. Her only friend is Lisette, a girl she meets in the cemetery. However, it turns out that Lisette is a ghost. She is limited to haunting the cemetery, the Bowman house, and her childhood home until her murder is avenged. This will occur with the end of the curse that was placed on the Bowm</span>
  <span id="freeText6051169393152168466" style="display:none">Rebbecca is sent to live with her Aunt in New Orleans when her dad has to travel to China for work. She knows no one here and is immediately put off by the snobbish manners of the girls she attends school with. Her only friend is Lisette, a girl she meets in the cemetery. However, it turns out that Lisette is a ghost. She is limited to haunting the cemetery, the Bowman house, and her childhood home until her murder is avenged. This will occur with the end of the curse that was placed on the Bowman family by Lisette's mother. The curse has been that every girl born to the Bowman family will die before they reach their seventeenth birthday. Six Bowman girls have died so far and one more must die before the curse will end. Two Bowman girls are about to turn seventeen, which will survive?<br />I really don't know what to say about this one. I can't seem to pinpoint exactly why I did not care for this book. I started out enjoying it but, as with many books I have read lately, it started disappointing me about midway through. As another reviewer here stated, about the only character that I liked and that I felt sympathy for was Lisette. I particularly did not like the ending. All anyone was concerned about was the curse ending as long as it was not them or someone in their family who would be the one to die to end it. How callous. And I find it equally disturbing that Anton burns the Bowman house down, and there are no repercussions. Wasn't Anton supposed to be one of the "good guys". Maybe that is part of the reason why I did not care for this one, there really were no "good guys". But I guess that makes it more realistic. Anyway, it was not a bad book, it just wasn't the best ghost story I have read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6051169393152168466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_142331202" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142331202" />
    <a title="Hope" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1768876-hope"><img alt="Hope" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578274685p2/1768876.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142331202?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hope" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hope" href="/user/show/1768876-hope">Hope</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1768876-hope?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1768876-hope?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1768876-hope?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1768876-hope?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1768876-hope?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1768876-hope?shelf=ghosts-and-haunted-houses">ghosts-and-haunted-houses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1768876-hope?shelf=snuggly-books-for-rainy-days">snuggly-books-for-rainy-days</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142331202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16974416780128525585">Given the fact that I only read this book because of the cover, I wasn’t really expecting much from it. <br/>Well, my expectations were exceeded. <br/><br/>I can probably count on one hand how many ghost stories I’ve read in my life. And this is a nice little ghostly tale set in New Orleans, a perfect little volume to curl up with when it’s cloudy and cold outside. Which is exactly what I did with it, and so maybe my feelings toward this little novel have been affected by the giant blizzard, but I <i>really</i> liked</span>
  <span id="freeText16974416780128525585" style="display:none">Given the fact that I only read this book because of the cover, I wasn’t really expecting much from it. <br />Well, my expectations were exceeded. <br /><br />I can probably count on one hand how many ghost stories I’ve read in my life. And this is a nice little ghostly tale set in New Orleans, a perfect little volume to curl up with when it’s cloudy and cold outside. Which is exactly what I did with it, and so maybe my feelings toward this little novel have been affected by the giant blizzard, but I <i>really</i> liked this. <br /><br />Paula Morris pulled me in with a decidedly creepy prologue, and then abruptly switched voices. It’s like there are two voices in this novel; one is dark and creepy, and the other is naïve and curious. Or something. I’m not really sure how to describe it. <br /><br />Over all, this is a <i>dark</i> story. What with curses, references to voodoo/black magic, and other things that I am totally uncomfortable with. I have to say that I’m glad it wasn’t all just “fake” in the end. I kind of like that it was real, because there <i>are</i> evil forces at work in this world. In every mystery or ghost story, it seems like it’s always discovered to be some sort of elaborate trick, which can be explained away with enough logic and reason. I rather liked that this wasn’t one of those stories. <br /><br />So yes, I was creeped out. And yes, it did seem kind of “out there” some times. But it was a fun read, all-in-all, and I thoroughly enjoyed it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16974416780128525585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_184143866" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184143866" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1222379-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242269090p2/1222379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184143866?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/1222379-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer184143866&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184143866" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10016157991567123676">Although this book deals with much about New Orleans that is exotic and otherworldly, the author does a marvelous job at describing what it's like to be an outsider in a society or culture that is very much closed to anyone who isn't one of the inner circle. When Rebecca Brown comes to live--reluctantly--in New Orleans three years after Hurricane Katrina, she knows very little about the place. The girls at her private school snub her, of course, and she ends up haunting the local cemetery where </span>
  <span id="freeText10016157991567123676" style="display:none">Although this book deals with much about New Orleans that is exotic and otherworldly, the author does a marvelous job at describing what it's like to be an outsider in a society or culture that is very much closed to anyone who isn't one of the inner circle. When Rebecca Brown comes to live--reluctantly--in New Orleans three years after Hurricane Katrina, she knows very little about the place. The girls at her private school snub her, of course, and she ends up haunting the local cemetery where she meets up with a ghost. There is much to enjoy about the book, particularly the flavors of this distinctive city that is so different from every other city in the United States, but my enjoyment of the story was ruined by that over-the-top ending: a kidnapping during a major parade and a planned shooting in the cemetery! There were details like that, and Rebecca's father's staying in New Orleans in secret just to watch over her or leaving the city to escape a curse, that just didn't ring true to me. It's a shame really since the author concocts such a rich slice of life in New Orleans with its troubled past and sometimes uncertain future. Still, this one deserves a read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10016157991567123676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Shiralea Woodhouse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/810559-shiralea-woodhouse"><img alt="Shiralea Woodhouse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203099631p2/810559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/141652129?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shiralea Woodhouse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shiralea Woodhouse" href="/user/show/810559-shiralea-woodhouse">Shiralea Woodhouse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/810559-shiralea-woodhouse?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141652129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12106095738560787552">I admit it - I picked up this book because it was set in Louisiana...and even better, in a graveyard in New Orleans. I (being a La. native) have always loved the aboveground cemeteries - there is just something "neat-o" about them! And the author managed to weave in some of the history and culture of N.O. into the story. So I enjoyed the setting. However: although I've never run into the "upper crust" of the garden district, it's a little hard to believe they would be SO snotty...and homicidal (</span>
  <span id="freeText12106095738560787552" style="display:none">I admit it - I picked up this book because it was set in Louisiana...and even better, in a graveyard in New Orleans. I (being a La. native) have always loved the aboveground cemeteries - there is just something "neat-o" about them! And the author managed to weave in some of the history and culture of N.O. into the story. So I enjoyed the setting. However: although I've never run into the "upper crust" of the garden district, it's a little hard to believe they would be SO snotty...and homicidal (most southerners are pretty nice! Look at me! lol!) The characters all felt a little one dimensional to me, which was disappointing, because I really liked the story line. It was interesting and fun with a good twist. But I also felt the end was missing something, and I had questions that didn't really get answered. OK - and here is another thing that bothered me: the "ghost" on the cover doesn't seem to be connected to the story. ?? My favorite part of this book: the "ghost walk" through N.O.!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12106095738560787552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText16408504405903247573" style="display:none">I'm probably being too generous with a 3 star rating, but I did like this book..... Interesting litte story, Welcome to New Orleans: City of Voodoo and Beauty. Of Hurricanes and Hauntings. <br />Main Character, Rebecca makes a friend in Lisette.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i90t9ejowmG1qBL3m+L66dQ4LImVhdpuB2brgr1DUd5nwxe9VyWa8Kkf/7HnliN0q6NSJjFO0ouXa+7sz+9X1A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4AgZEtBbralr7nY7+he99txEKzFbhqOWKrYKdNzmEAMMFiNab5b1OHdZm32GY2Rro99Vnv9Nq3O6uw8arkoWCQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2692163880560399278">Paula Morris, a novelist and short story writer of English and Maori descent, was born in New Zealand. For almost a decade she worked in the record business in London and New York. She now lives in New Orleans, where she teaches creative writing at Tulane University.<br/><br/>Paula's first novel, Queen of Beauty, won best first work of fiction at the 2003 Montana New Zealand Book Awards. Hibiscus Coast, a l</span>
  <span id="freeText2692163880560399278" style="display:none">Paula Morris, a novelist and short story writer of English and Maori descent, was born in New Zealand. For almost a decade she worked in the record business in London and New York. She now lives in New Orleans, where she teaches creative writing at Tulane University.<br /><br />Paula's first novel, Queen of Beauty, won best first work of fiction at the 2003 Montana New Zealand Book Awards. Hibiscus Coast, a literary thriller set in Auckland and Shanghai, was published in 2005 and has been optioned for film. Her third novel, Trendy But Casual, was published by Penguin New Zealand in 2005.<br /><br />Paula's first short story collection, Forbidden Cities (2008) was a regional finalist in the 2009 Commonwealth Writers' Prize.<br /><br />Ruined, her first YA novel, was published by Scholastic in 2009.</span>
